#studies‚úçüèº

so what if a Y4 with 4.1 GPA says that your Y1/2 GPA of 3.8 sucks? likewise, so what if a Y3 with a 3.2 GPA says that your Y1/2 GPA of 3.3 is ok? its dumb asking if your GPA is good, or okay, or if you're 'cooked'.

that depends on your own standards, your own aspirations, your own efforts, your own circumstances, your own abilities, and how well you fit the mods you took.

if you got a 3.5 and you want a summa, worked super hard, had no challenging circumstances, didnt wake up on the wrong side of bed on exam day, and took mods that played to your strengths, then by your own expectations and situation, its fine to feel disappointed, but thereafter you should recalibrate expectations downwards, or find some way to be more efficient/effective next sem to push your next sem upwards.

if you got a 3.1 and just want at least a merit and to get uni done with, didnt work really hard, had challenging circumstances, woke up on the wrong side of bed on exam day, took mods that didnt play to your strengths, then it follows that, well, you should just be a chill guy.

only you will know whether youve done well (enough) based on your means and desires. stop living for external validation, you live with only yourself at the end of the day.

#studies‚úçüèº

Honestly, this semester has been my best due to all mods being my strengths, which is a good thing. But the true joy was seeing most of my friends and students doing well in the end, seeing their struggles, coaching/tutoring them and finally seeing my effort come to fruition. I've been helping others since Y1 but it was a massacre and it feels bad doing well while the people you're helping don't, it made me doubt my teaching abilities, but this sem, has been the best for me because I finally feel like a teacher. It has confirmed my interest to continue being a TA for as many modules as possible and to be an educator. This is true joy, it's not about my grades but the understanding of the module I seek to become a better teacher and to see my students and friends succeed.

For those whose thoughts resonate with mine, I hope you'll become a TA in the future! It was a great sem teaching, I'll never forget the fun and struggles we had on telegram and during my office hours :)

Just wanted to get this off my chest, since I can't bring myself to tell my students the same thing without getting emotional. We need passionate teachers and I hope that I've inspired some of them to give back to the modules I no longer TA for.

Some firms, such as JPMC don‚Äôt ask for GPA anymore. They care more about your HireVue performance. They‚Äôre also one of the biggest advocates for diversity hires so if you fit into that profile, higher chance.

Others like MS, GS, and BofA still ask for it, but there seems to be less emphasis on it. For context, my GPA was way below the recommended threshold (3.5 and up) but I still got interviews from all 3. Just make sure your Resume has something to make it stand out (Internships, Projects, Hackathons, Awards)

#studies‚úçüèº

#S12200143 cont.

but if youre still that desperate to know where you stand relatively, there are three things you that may help:

(1): the median grade in SMU is probably a B+ (3.3) or B (3.0), given that As are broadly capped at 30%. so the perfectly average student is probably somewhere within that range, if theyre consistently average, but this depends a little based on school, of course.

(2): scholars need to maintain a 3.4 GPA, which normatively signals what is minimally acceptable for a student that is deemed by the school of being worthy of additional investment.

(2): and you want a good sense of the honours distribution for each school specifically, you can watch previous years' commencement videos. they announce everyone's honour classification after their name and degree programme (but stopped this year). trust me, i was as desperate for external validation once, and i watched the law one (the shortest). for the llb '22, 142 attended: 18 (12%) SCL; 36 (25%) MCL; 52 (35%) CL; 40 (27%) others/none. this breakdown excludes those who did not attend, which might skew in a certain way, and definitely also varies by school and attendance.

all this relative performance, again, doesnt matter, though, and comparison is always the thief of joy: i say this as a graduating y5 scholar on a ddp and a 3.98, who once felt really dissappointed that i would not end with a perfect 4.0 whilst many around me did. everyone has their own goals and runs their own race, why should you let my (likewise any other) opinion colour how you feel about your own gpa.

you free yourself when you realise what someone else feels about your decimal points doesnt determine your worth or self image unless you let it be that way.

for yall clueless year 1s who needa be spoon fed information....


i-grade is only for those who are unable to take their finals/all the components and chooses to do it the next semester the module is offered. you have to apply for it if you miss your finals within 24-48 hours with VALID MC. and it's ultimately subjected to school's approval


s/u, you only can s/u exploratory modules upon filing for graduation

YOU CANNOT REDO / I-GRADE A MOD JUST BECAUSE YOU DIDNT DO WELL bruh. you only can retake if you get F

IF YOU DUNNO PLEASE READ YOUR HANDBOOK.

18:26
#studies‚úçüèº

Appeals:
For those submitting appeals, its not gonna work if you don't actually have receipts (eg: proof in writing that there's been instructor discrimination/your class part is unfairly tabulated). The moderation/tabulation of components are mostly automated too, so there's very little chance of error, your instructor will probably just relook to see if any manual inputs were keyed incorrectly. Other pleas really do not work, and will cost you literally and figuratively -- its $15/module appeal, and the form will ask you for the number of appeals you are submitting this semester, and for how many unsuccessful appeals you have made in the past. Frivoulous appeals today will count against you in the future, so only appeal if there's an obvious grading error. As you can imagine its pretty much also a black box, so you'll really need a watertight case, the school is not going to come back to you with more questions. If you're slightly under average you may already be a B/B-, so don't be too surprised.

I-Grades:
As for I-Grades, lol read your academic handbook. That's for circumstances in which you are unable to take the finals, and that form would have had to be submitted pretty much the moment you know you weren't taking the final. So its not retrospective, and you would've had to take the final the next sem anyway

#studies‚úçüèº

For those that want to appeal, do know that even if your Prof approves the appeal and is willing to bump you up the school makes the final decision.

The school will also look through everything submitted by you and grading by your Prof before deciding on whether you deserve to get that extra credit. Only obvious errors or discrimination by Profs will get you bump up.

Otherwise, just save your $15 and use it somewhere more useful.

#adviceüó£Ô∏è

Recent smu grad here. Ive had a history of being a jokester since secondary sch (and still am as a working adult). I have seen too many troll/joke posts here, thats fine and all.

I guess these can be the unofficial code of honor for trolling:

1) When we troll, make sure no one is hurt/offended/harmed in anyway. Once someone is hurt or offended, it defeats the purpose of trolling cus we are supposed to make ppl laugh and not sour their mood

2) beware of bringing up certain topics when trolling (best to avoid doing these altogether). Anything related to religion, mental health, suicide, self harm, sexuality and etc should NOT be included in any form of troll/jokes cus sensitive (we are supposed to respect these, not mindlessly offend ppl)

3) see who ur target audience is (some people may get offended by certain topics so yea)

4) see ur surroundings (at certain places, some jokes arent allowed)

In Y2S1, I had a bad sem and got a GPA around 2 (had 2 Ds), which pulled my entire CGPA to 2.99.

It felt like the world ended really but the next sem I grinded really hard and got a 4.0 and then 3.74 now ‚Äî so my CGPA has been saved to 3.38.

Don‚Äôt feel like your life is over because you had a bad GPA; just remember i) if you have time, it can always be saved, ii) no one really cares and if, they do, iii) you will find a way e.g., jobs, internships, because life in SG is just so tough that you WILL eventually figure it out, even if it takes longer

Stop worrying and have a good December break before the next semester starts again :-)

#adviceüó£Ô∏è

TWO takeaways from receiving GPA results:

1. Don't cry over spilt milk

it's perfectly normal to be discontented with your grades. in fact, it really sucks when miss the mark just by a bit. however, no matter how much you whine or sulk, you wont magically get a 4.0 GPA. yes, you might be upset because your peer scored better than you. yes, you might be upset because you put in so much effort only to receive a C. but grades, after all, are just mere letters. when you go out and find a job next time, they will care more than your grades alone.

2. Be contented with what you have

Just like me, my first instinct was to appeal for one of my mods (CS101) because i did not receive my desired grade. but after witnessing someone's grade taking a turn for the worse after appealing, I have learnt to be satisfied with my own grades. living in SG is a never ending rat-race, but we just gotta embrace what we have, and what lies ahead of us

character which is disciplined enough to put in the work

with much more difficult circumstances in the past and yet
achieve stellar results. Most importantly, even though I am
the one who will benefit the most, it was not a solo show,
without my friends, I would definitely have not achieved
this. Without Shaun, I would have not gotten an A+ for my

#love‚ù§Ô∏è

For the guys out there, getting a date/talking to girls isn't complicated. Even if you aren't that tall, or rich, or good looking.

Some advice (which applies to both being a decent human being, and generally attractive)

1) Be observant: notice when she puts in effort (e.g., makeup, new jewelry etc.) And compliment said effort. It costs u nothing. Even better is if you can notice when people are upset/sad, it's not hard - a change in texting patterns, choice of words, tonality, body language etc.

2) Be emotionally available: Being attuned to your own emotions generally means you can empathise with others. Stop making your modus operandi be offer a solution, listen first, understand their emotions, and keep your mouth shut.

3) Be interesting Stop making your life be about your job, or gym, studies etc. Talk about different things, hypothetical situations, fiction stories etc. And stop talking about yourself so much, ask more questions, let people speak about their own passions and genuinely be interested in it.

4) Be courageous show the girl you care more for her than every other girl (maybe except ur siblings/mum) in your life. Take like 5 minutes to Google good date ideas (ChatGPT exists...), show her you want to take this further than a friendship. Half the time a friendzone exists cos guys don't bother trying to step out of it. If she rejects you, just move on.

As to "simping" - there's nothing wrong with treating a girl like a princess. But what most people dislike is when you "lose yourself" and forget what made you unique.

Everything else generally is a matter of preference: looks, hobbies, values, lifestyle etc.

Many ways to tell if a girl likes you but but

1) If she puts in effort / makes in abundantly clear she likes spending time (1:1) with you. E.g., you propose a date and she carves out time to meet u

2) she happily replies your texts / prioritises replying them when she can. Not everyone can reply instantly, but no one really needs like 12h to reply to someone they like.

3) She is physically close to you when both of you go out. Like much closer than she would be with other guy friends.

4) She responds in a flirtatious manner alot.

Okay regardless, if ur unsure, just go confess. Plan a date, make sure she knows its a date, and try your luck :) at least, even if u get rejected, you can find some closure
